# Orchestrator journal archive -- 2026-06

Decisions rotated out of `data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json` (oldest first within each batch; newest overall is in the live journal). Source of truth for "why we did X" once it ages past the live tail. See also git log + the GitHub releases.

## 2026-06-16

**Decision:** MULTIPLAYER CO-PRESENCE (v0.472.0) + BATTERY SoC (v0.473.0). (1) v0.472.0 CO-PRESENCE: built out the client wiring so two players share the VPS world (operator has a tester lined up). Discovery: the RELAY half is essentially DONE -- handle_game_join (msg_handlers.rs:3276) spawns + welcomes + broadcasts game_player_joined, and handle_game_position_update (3395) VALIDATES (anti-teleport) + BROADCASTS game_position_update to all clients. The gap was 100% client-side, so this is a CLIENT-ONLY change (zero relay risk). Reused the EXISTING authenticated chat WebSocket (gui_state.ws_client) per first-playable.md -- no second socket, no second auth (the wrong-wire-format NetClient is NOT used). Wired: on entering the 3D world while connected, send {type:game_join, player_name, character_mode:'local'} once (character_mode reserved for the open/closed-server model from day one), then stream {type:game_position_update,...} ~15/sec from the camera; route __game__: traffic (game_welcome via private, game_player_joined/game_position_update/game_player_left via system) into NetSyncSystem instead of discarding it at lib.rs:4264; NetSyncSystem (now actually instantiated + ticked fully-qualified via the System trait) spawns/moves/despawns RemotePlayer entities + interpolates; render a teal humanoid marker (body box + head sphere) per remote at its interpolated position. Robustness: self-filter (relay echoes our own join/pos -> skip our player_id from game_welcome + despawn self spawned in the race); join-order-independent (a PositionUpdate for an unknown player lazy-spawns them, so an already-present player appears on their next move). DEFER: nameplates, world-snapshot prefill, the full character launcher (Play->launcher flow + multi-save switching + persistence + networked server sections -- GUI-heavy + needs the operator's visual confirm, not crammed blind). The character/server design (incl. the launcher requirements) is captured in docs/design/characters-and-servers.md. (2) v0.473.0 BATTERY SoC (live-home-sim 1b): new Battery component {charge_wh,capacity_wh,max_charge_w,max_discharge_w} + MachinePower::Battery; the 8 battery_bank instances in home.ron now carry power: Some(Battery(4kWh, 2kW in/out)) and spawn live (half-charged). ElectricalSystem integrates the grid balance (gen-demand) into each bank via a PURE unit-tested integrate_battery() (charge on surplus, discharge on deficit, clamped by capacity + rates), publishes battery_wh/capacity/autonomy_hours into PowerStatus; the HUD draws a live 'Battery: N%  X kWh  ~H h autonomy' line under the power line, so the day/night solar swing is now a draining/refilling number not a static string. native+relay compile; 446 lib tests pass (3 new battery tests); 4 GUI lints green. NOTE: battery does not yet PREVENT load-shedding (it tracks the true gen-vs-demand balance); unifying discharge with the shed loop is a follow-up.

**Why:** Operator: build out the multiplayer (tester coming) + keep building the queue. Co-presence is the #1 goal and the relay half was already done, so the client wiring (client-only, no prod-relay risk) was the right, verifiable build; shipped so the operator can give the tester the new client. Kept the full character LAUNCHER for a focused pass (it is egui-flow-heavy + save-switching + persistence, which I cannot visually verify and should not rush). Then advanced the queue with Battery SoC -- pure ECS, fully unit-testable, makes the home sim's power loop consequential -- to keep building with correctness intact.

**Files:** src/lib.rs, src/net/sync.rs, src/systems/electrical.rs, src/ecs/components.rs, src/machines.rs, data/machines/home.ron, src/gui/pages/hud.rs, src/gui/mod.rs


## 2026-06-16

**Decision:** BUILD PASS (operator: multiplayer + character selector primary; also do multistory, structural spike, web a11y; then sync the roadmap). SHIPPED + VERIFIED: (1) v0.471.0 MULTISTORY EDITOR -- RoomConfig.level + HomesteadLayout.story_height (serde-default, byte-identical RON); world Y = level*story_height in resolve_positions; the A2 landmine FIXED: find_shared_edges is now Y-aware (requires vertical overlap) so stacked rooms never register as wall-sharing + never cut doors into floors, and a storey-spanning room (the mall) neighbours both bands; editor gets a Level stepper (left panel filters the tree to the active floor + new rooms land there), a per-room Storey stepper, and the 2D plan shows one floor. (2) v0.471.0 STRUCTURAL DE-RISK SPIKE -- new src/systems/construction/solver.rs, a pure (glam+std, relay-safe, unit-tested) node-beam model: load routes to ground via a hop-distance field, overloaded members break, breaks cascade, disconnected nodes are flood-filled as islands; wired into structural.rs::StructuralResult; tests prove an intact ~200-member frame stands and pulling one of three posts cascades (2 break) -> islands the beam -> Collapsed. (3) v0.471.0 WEB ACCESSIBILITY -- the dead accessibility.js/i18n.js/glossary.js (loaded by 0 of 38 pages while the landing promised them) now load from shell.js on every page + the Settings toggles apply/persist/reflect; added a Colorblind select + backing CSS; removed the broken Deutsch option (no de.json). 443 lib tests pass, native+relay compile, 4 GUI lints green. MULTIPLAYER + CHARACTER SELECTOR (the primary): NOT built this pass -- it is a large, high-stakes arc (production relay + a 2-client test I cannot run + a launcher redesign + multi-character wiring), so per the correctness-over-cramming rule I captured the FULL design instead (incl. the operator's new launcher requirements: Play->launcher, default-character checkbox to skip select, offline character editor anytime, a server changing-station to gate mid-expedition cosmetic swaps, section order Homes/local-open/closed) into docs/design/characters-and-servers.md, and left it as the top-of-queue NEXT arc. The save infra (persistence::list_saves, save/load) exists but is not wired into the single-active-home Play flow; first increment = offline multi-character launcher. ROADMAP SYNC (operator asked): updated docs/ROADMAP.md with everything shipped (construction arc, website parity, security+signing, multistory/structural/a11y) marked [done], the multiplayer/character arc as [next], and the 12 novel ideas as [future] across themes; regenerated data/roadmap.json (renders to app+website); migrated the not-done items + fixed the PRIORITIES/STATUS pointers to ROADMAP; DELETED the one-off docs/history/2026-06-16-rest-of-day-plan.md (the roadmap is now the single planning doc). Signing P0 RESOLVED (operator signed v0.470.0, check-signing green).

**Why:** Operator wanted a big multi-feature pass. Delivered the three self-contained, verifiable features (multistory, structural spike, web a11y) to a shipped + tested bar. Did NOT cram multiplayer co-presence: it touches the production relay + cannot be 2-client-verified by me + needs a launcher/multi-character redesign, so a rushed version would violate the operator's equal requirement to double-check + not sacrifice correctness for speed. Captured its full design (with the new launcher requirements) so the next focused pass builds it right -- the join wire must carry the character dimension from day one. Synced the roadmap as the single canonical planning doc per the operator's explicit instruction.

**Files:** src/ship/fibonacci.rs, src/gui/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/construction.rs, src/lib.rs, src/systems/construction/solver.rs, src/systems/construction/structural.rs, web/shared/shell.js, web/pages/settings-app.js, web/pages/settings.html, docs/ROADMAP.md, data/roadmap.json, docs/design/characters-and-servers.md


## 2026-06-16

**Decision:** CHARACTER + SERVER MODEL captured (operator requirement for multiplayer): self-custodial LOCAL characters vs SERVER-HELD authoritative characters, with servers declaring open/closed/hybrid policy = Diablo II open vs closed Battle.net. Designed via a 4-agent workflow grounded in the actual code; written to docs/design/characters-and-servers.md + cross-linked from first-playable.md. KEY MODEL: a character is TWO decoupled objects. (1) IDENTITY + COSMETICS (Dilithium key + name/appearance/outfit/design) = ALWAYS self-custodial; promote the existing WorldSave cosmetic fields (persistence.rs:14-48) to a new character_v1 signed object via the existing ObjectBuilder (object.rs), replicates over gossip like signed_profiles. (2) PROGRESSION (skills/XP/inventory/currency/reputation/quests) = owned per server policy; on a CLOSED server the relay is sole writer. Most machinery ALREADY EXISTS: PlayerProgress keyed by pubkey (game_persistence.rs:67-82), handle_game_join re-seeds from it + never trusts client stats (msg_handlers.rs:3303), apply_quest_reward computes XP server-side (game_state.rs:757). Server policy = a character_policy field (default 'open') on ServerInfoResponse + FederatedServerEntry. Character-select UI splits showroom draw_character_select (showroom.rs:79) into a LOCAL section (saves/) + per-server SERVER sections (GET /api/characters), honest greying per policy. LOAD-BEARING for first-playable: the game_join envelope MUST carry character_mode + (character bytes | character_id) from day one (can't retrofit), identity must derive from the identify-bound socket key not the client player_name, and character_policy must exist on ServerInfoResponse before the selector renders. Everything else (server_characters table with stats_json/inventory_json, N-per-realm, intent-based inventory mutation) defers until after first co-presence -- the single player_progress row suffices for the first slice. Operator forks resolved with reasonable defaults (closed-server may opt-in to force fresh cosmetics; open-server self-custodied-progression is a per-server opt-in flag defaulting to cosmetics-only; 'real' sensor-home custody deferred). 7-step build order captured. ALSO answered the sign-release SOP (verified: release-signing-key.enc present, pubkeys provisioned, v0.470.0 Build-Desktop succeeded -> signable; operator just runs `just sign-release v0.470.0` with the passphrase exported).

**Why:** Operator flagged this as a multiplayer requirement and it shapes the very first join wire, so capturing it now (grounded, not hand-wavy) prevents a costly retrofit -- the join envelope and the server-authoritative trust boundary have to be right on day one. Used a workflow to ground it in the real identity/relay/profile code; the standout finding is that the self-custody/anti-cheat split maps almost 1:1 onto systems that already exist (signed objects for identity, player_progress + never-trust-client-stats for closed progression), so it's mostly naming + wiring, not new machinery. Design capture only -- multiplayer is not being built yet; this is the spec for when it is.

**Files:** docs/design/characters-and-servers.md, docs/design/first-playable.md

Deliverables shipped (commit f17c1bb7, docs/tooling only, no behaviour change): (1) docs/history/2026-06-16-rest-of-day-plan.md = the full decision-ready menu; (2) docs/design/first-playable.md = the verified multiplayer co-presence gap list; (3) scripts/check-release-signing.js wired into `just status` + a new `just check-signing` + a P1 alert in HEALTH-DASHBOARD.md; (4) PRIORITIES P0 banner + plan pointer; (5) STATUS.md header refreshed v0.416.0->v0.469.3. TWO VERIFIED FINDINGS: (A) P0 -- NO release from v0.421.0..v0.469.0 carries release-manifest.json.sig.json (verified via gh release view), so the enforce-mode desktop updater (updater.rs MANIFEST_SIG_NAME, refuses unsigned) has offered NOTHING for ~48 releases. Desktop auto-update is silently dead. Fix = operator-only `just sign-release` (signing the latest carries all prior changes). (B) The #1 near-term goal (playable multiplayer on the VPS) was NEVER wired on the client: relay game world is LIVE (handle_game_join, msg_handlers.rs:3276) but NetSyncSystem/NetClient are referenced 0 times in lib.rs, and lib.rs:4264 filters __game__: out of CHAT without ever routing it into the world; plus protocol drift NetMessage{Join} vs relay{game_join}. NOVEL IDEAS captured (12): FederationBundle (signed-object bundle over USB/QR/LoRa/sneakernet -- the latent superpower 4 other ideas snap onto), Skill Passport (offline-verifiable PQ proof-of-competence), Build-It-For-Real (BOM->group-buy), Offline Survival Codex, schema-driven in-app Make-a-Thing editor, Time-Bank, Generation-Ship co-op pilot, AI Mentor Sage (scripted-fallback, no LLM), Disaster Mode, open sensor protocol (ESP32->home-sim), Mission Pulse (federated aggregate-only impact dashboard), Continuity Capsule (Shamir succession). Also ran the overdue cargo-audit (separate entry/result). Did NOT build feature work or pick an arc -- left the menu for the operator.

**Why:** Operator explicitly scoped this to PLANNING + novel ideas, so the deliverable is a decision-ready plan, not a direction commitment. Used a workflow because the task spans the whole project; verified the two findings by hand because the watchouts warned not to over-trust subagents (STATUS.md checkmarks are self-flagged unverified pre-v0.132). Surfaced the silent signing P0 with a permanent automated check so it can never recur unnoticed. Limited my own 'doing' to safe, direction-agnostic hygiene (docs, the signing check, cargo-audit) -- feature/spike choices (multistory, structural solver, home-sim battery, web a11y wiring, multiplayer wiring) are the operator's to pick from the menu.

## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** WEB-PARITY FOLLOW-UPS v0.469.2/.3 + a SERVICE-WORKER CACHE LESSON. After v0.469.1 shipped the website landing = app Mission Dashboard + header = app nav, the operator reported 'the website didn't change' even after hard refreshes. ROOT CAUSE: the service worker (web/shared/sw.js) precached shell.js/theme.css and served them CACHE-FIRST, so a deployed shell.js (the nav) stayed hidden behind the old cached copy until a full SW reinstall - even though the server sends shell.js with `no-cache, must-revalidate` and the HTML with `no-store` (verified live via curl: the new landing + new shell.js WERE on the server the whole time). FIX v0.469.2: switched the SHELL_URLS to NETWORK-FIRST with cache fallback (online -> fresh ETag-revalidated fetch; offline -> cached), so web deploys now appear on the next normal reload. The definitive way to verify a web deploy past any client cache is an INCOGNITO/private window (no SW, no shared cache) - curl proves the server, incognito proves the client. v0.469.3: the v0.469.1 header had TWO Humanity entries (the old green-bordered 'H' brand logo AND a new Humanity tab) -> removed the standalone brand (the app has no logo); the leading Humanity tab (orange 'H' mark + label) is the single home button. Also fixed nav-group colour bars (theme.css tints each tab red/green/blue by its nav-group wrapper): regrouped into 3 clean contiguous blocks - RED = platform entry (Play, Humanity, Chat, Studio), GREEN = your stuff (Profile, Home, Quests, Tasks, Inventory, Crafting, Map), BLUE = system (Platform, Library, Settings). All web-only patch bumps. NOTE: browser preview tool was denied this session, so web changes were verified by code review + live curl, not a rendered preview.

**Why:** Operator's 'website didn't change' was a service-worker cache-first trap, not a deploy failure - a recurring class of bug worth remembering: SW cache-first on shell assets silently hides web deploys. Network-first respects the server's revalidate headers and self-heals. The duplicate-H + colour-block issues were real defects in the v0.469.1 nav rewrite (an unneeded brand logo + arbitrary colour grouping); fixed to match the app's single-Humanity, clean-block look.

**Files:** web/shared/sw.js, web/shared/shell.js

## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** v0.469.0 OPENINGS AS PLACED OBJECTS - redesigned the door/window system after the operator said the v0.468 wall-kind model was unintuitive ('we need a better way... we don't want the wall to go away, we want to ADD a door/airlock/window to a specific spot'). Designed via a 5-agent + synthesis workflow, implemented the verified plan. DATA: new OpeningKind{Door,Window,Airlock,Hatch} + Opening{wall:u8,kind,u,v,w,h,profile:Option<String>} + RoomConfig.openings:Vec<Opening> (#[serde(default, skip_serializing_if=Vec::is_empty)] so shipped RON is byte-identical, all prior tests green). build_meshes appends each room's openings to the SAME per-opening tuple list OUTSIDE the WallKind match (5-tuple now carries a per-opening glazed flag), so a plain Solid wall is cut where an object sits + stays solid elsewhere; free centre-height v maps to sill=v-h/2 the glass/casing already speak; multiple per wall already work (wall_with_openings loops spans). GIZMO (3D): rewrote to ray-vs-wall-PLANE (walls are vertical) -> (u along, v up); opening_handles returns a move handle + 4 edge resize handles per placed non-floor opening; try_begin_room_grab/apply_gizmo_drag do Move (door u+floor-snap; window u+v) and Resize (edge-anchored, min 0.3m), all clamped; move cube=accent, resize cubes=warning, floated proud toward camera. EDITOR: right pane now an Openings list (Add Door/Window/Airlock buttons + per-opening kind/wall combos + Along/Up/W/H DragValues whose .range() is the LIVE wall length+ceiling -> the 20m-vs-2m decouple is gone) + per-frame reclamp after a room resize; wall combos dropped Door/Window (now objects), keep Solid/Auto/Open/Mirror. BACK-COMPAT: legacy WallKind::Door/Window faces still render + slide (handles opening_index=None write WallSet.offsets) so opening_handles_track_wall_offset passes byte-for-byte; added promote_walls_to_openings (editor-only) to convert a legacy face to an Opening + demote to Solid. GARDEN BUG (operator: 'disconnected study from garden, the garden never regenerated its wall'): root cause = adjacency-dependent wall EXISTENCE (Open consulted no adjacency = sticky gap; neighbor_owns ownership-transfer flickered in find_shared_edges' 0.15m/0.5m dead-band). Fixed structurally: Open self-heals to Solid with no passable neighbour; neighbor_owns never suppresses a wall that owns a placed opening. native+relay compile; 437 lib tests pass incl 9 NEW opening tests (cut-on-solid, free-height glass, two-per-wall, u+v clamp, door floor-snap, round-trip, empty-not-serialized, legacy-promote, open-reseal); 4 GUI/theme lints green.

**Why:** Operator rejected the v0.468 wall-kind model as unintuitive and listed concrete gaps: can't add more windows, can't resize, door always centred, the slide number lied (20m on a 2m wall), and a disconnected wall didn't reseal. The object-on-solid-wall model fixes all of them AND structurally kills the garden bug (wall existence no longer depends on adjacency). Used a workflow for the adversarially-verified plan because it spanned data model + wall-plane gizmo math + editor UX + migration; kept legacy faces working so shipped RON + all tests stay green. SVG/curved cutouts (Opening.profile) reserved for Stage 2.

**Files:** src/ship/fibonacci.rs, src/lib.rs, src/gui/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/construction.rs, docs/design/construction-architecture.md


## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** v0.468.0 DOOR/WINDOW SLIDE GIZMO - the editor slice the operator asked for ('a little gizmo at the base of the door, in the center, that the user can click on and slide along the wall'). Data: WallSet gained offsets:[f32;4] (signed metres along each wall N/S/W/E; #[serde(default)] so old RON loads [0;4]; honoured only for explicit Door/Window walls). build_meshes adds the offset to the opening center_t - a Door's base is still the nearest passable shared edge (a pinned door stays in its doorway until slid), a Window's base is the wall centre; both clamped inside the wall. NEW fibonacci::opening_handles(layout,positions) -> Vec<OpeningHandle> mirrors that center_t maths (incl. the door base + the 'neighbour owns the shared wall' skip) so a handle sits exactly on each movable opening of the SELECTED room. lib.rs: draws each handle as a small glowing accent cube (transparent pass, cached mesh+material); left-click hit-tests handles BEFORE the room grab (ray vs floor plane, forgiving 0.35 m pick radius); a grabbed handle (ConstructionGizmoGrab) slides along its captured wall line (project cursor floor-hit onto the wall axis, offset = proj_t - base_t, snap 10 cm, clamp); held handle suppresses the room grab; released on mouse-up + on leaving the editor. construction.rs details pane also shows a numeric 'slide' DragValue + 'Center' reset per Door/Window wall (dual input). Reconcile copies wall_offsets into layout.rooms (both upsert + append branches) so it saves to RON. ALSO applied the locked terminology: left panel header 'Structure' (top-level container = home/mall/ship/base) over 'Home' (its rooms). native+relay compile, 7 fibonacci tests pass (NEW opening_handles_track_wall_offset: +0.7 m slides the bedroom north window handle +0.7 m along +X, stays on the wall line), 4 GUI/theme lints pass.

**Why:** Operator after the 3-column layout: wants to slide doors/windows along their wall via an in-view handle (non-centred doors, build-order step 3 in construction-architecture.md (g)). Built it on the existing pick_ray + reconcile + rebuild path the room grab already proved; kept the door's shared-edge default so existing layouts are unchanged at offset 0. Numeric field added alongside for keyboard-precise placement + because native egui can't be auto-verified (operator confirms the 3D handle). Terminology 'Structure' locked via AskUserQuestion in the prior turn.

**Files:** src/ship/fibonacci.rs, src/lib.rs, src/gui/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/construction.rs, docs/design/construction-architecture.md

## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** v0.466.0 3D ROOM GRAB - the slice that makes the astral editor a real builder. Mapped via a 5-agent workflow then implemented the verified plan. Camera::pick_ray(cursor,viewport) unprojects through inverse view-proj (reverse-Z: near=clip z 1, far=0) -> world ray, all modes. Left-press in construction (gated !egui_consumed; left is a no-op in the orbit cam so we own it) casts the ray, hit-tests each room's FLOOR rect (plane y=room_bounds.min.y, footprint from the AABB), selects+grabs nearest, stores grab offset (no jump). Per-frame apply_room_drag intersects the ray with the grabbed floor plane, moves the room to follow the cursor minus offset, snap 0.25, construction_dirty -> same reconcile+rebuild_homestead as the 2D canvas. Computed from live cursor not deltas (no drift). Selection highlight = translucent accent quad over the floor via the transparent pass, built once + cached (survives rebuild). KEY VERIFIED FACT: room_bounds order == homestead_floors order == construction_rooms by id, so one index reaches all three. New: Camera::pick_ray; EngineState cursor_pos/construction_grab/construction_hilite; GuiState.construction_selected_room; ConstructionGrab struct; CursorMoved arm. native+relay compile, 6 fibonacci tests pass, 4 GUI/theme lints pass.

**Why:** Operator 'then let's proceed' after the camera remap; the 3D grab is what turns fly-around+edit-numbers into a real builder. Reuses the proven 2D-canvas rebuild path; left-click was already reserved by the v0.465 remap.

**Files:** src/renderer/camera.rs, src/lib.rs, src/gui/mod.rs


## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** v0.465.0 orbit-cam remap + F1 keymap overlay. (1) CAMERA REMAP (operator) in camera.rs update_orbit (free-orbit/construction path): MIDDLE-drag=orbit (was left/right), RIGHT-drag=pan (was middle), pan now along the FLOOR plane (forward_xz + horizontal right) not screen-up. LEFT reserved for interaction/3D room grab. ## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** v0.460.0 - FIX the recurring 'UI shows but cannot interact' bug (showroom, then construction editor). Root cause: the cursor grab had FOUR authorities - the per-frame reconciliation PLUS the Escape page-transition handler, the inventory I-key, and a post-egui-frame page-change block - and the latter three called set_cursor_grab/set_cursor_visible directly WITHOUT updating cached state.cursor_free. That desynced the flag, so the reconciliation's `want != cursor_free` transition check no-opped (thought cursor already free when actually grabbed) -> cursor stayed captured for FPS look while a panel was open -> egui got no pointer -> panel rendered but un-clickable. FIX: ONE authority - new fn reconcile_cursor(state) computes want_free from active_page/showroom/construction, applies + updates cursor_free, and is the ONLY place that touches the cursor; called every frame AND right after the egui frame (catches egui-click page changes without a frame lag). Deleted the 3 stray grab/free sites. SOP: added INTERACTABILITY item #7 to Button/Action Wiring Checklist (operator directive) - wire new in-world egui surfaces into reconcile_cursor, block mouse-look, draw inside egui_ctx.run, and ASK the operator to confirm a click lands (native egui is un-verifiable from the harness). Wrote memory feedback_ui_interactability.md. native+relay compile.

**Why:** Operator: 'I can see the UI but cannot interact. This keeps being a problem. Add it to the SOP so when you add something you double check it for interactability.' The desync was the recurring root cause; single-authority reconcile_cursor fixes the whole class. Can't auto-verify native clicks from here, so SOP now mandates explicit operator confirmation.

**Files:** src/lib.rs, docs/SOP.md

## 2026-06-15

**Decision:** CONSTRUCTION ARCHITECTURE designed (docs/design/construction-architecture.md). Operator wants the build system to support NON-GRID/organic shapes (alien ships), GENERATE realistic structure (studs/joists/sheathing) from a simple boundary, test REAL physics loads, and be DESTRUCTIBLE (blow a hole + consequences like decompression). Ran a 6-agent research workflow (voxel/grid, SDF/organic, procedural-framing, structural-physics, hybrid/room) -> synthesis. DECISION: a 5-LAYER PIPELINE: (0) Rooms = derived semantic view (today RoomInfo+RoomTypeRegistry+EnclosedSpace, untouched); (1) Boundary = an editable planar WALL-GRAPH (DCEL/half-edge), B-rep-flavored, NOT voxel + NOT polygon-soup - bounding box today, oriented WallSpec next, organic wall-graph + optional SDF outer-hull later; (2) Generator = deterministic boundary->node-beam framing (studs/plates/headers/joists/sheathing via floating-repeat + opening sub-grammar, from materials.ron real strengths); (3) Physics-proxy = node-beam support-propagation solver (event-driven, red/green overlay) + flood-fill island detection for destruction -> rapier debris; (4) Render = instanced members + existing HomesteadMeshes. Destruction = boolean subtract on boundary -> re-solve -> islands fall -> breach flips EnclosedSpace.sealed -> existing AtmosphereSystem decompression (zero new survival code). Grounded in existing stubs (construction/{structural,csg,routing}.rs) + atmosphere.rs + materials.ron (verified present). 6-STEP plan: 1 room placement editor (WallSpec, near-term), 2 framing generator, 3 structural solver+overlay, 4 destruction+debris+decompression, 5 DCEL non-grid, 6 SDF hull. PROTOTYPE-FIRST de-risk: (a) node-beam solver+flood-fill on a hand-built framed wall+floor; (b) framing generator on a 30-deg off-axis wall. Pure geometry/data stays feature-agnostic (relay-buildable, unit-testable).

**Why:** Operator explicitly asked to figure out wall placement + structural elements, surveying existing options, with hard requirements (organic, realistic structure, physics, destruction). The wall-graph boundary keeps room placement (bounding box) as slice 1 while NOT boxing out organic - the do-it-right-first-time the operator wants. Researched not memory-only (Ultracode).

**Files:** docs/design/construction-architecture.md, docs/design/room-purpose-architecture.md

## 2026-06-14

**Decision:** MILKY WAY BAND (v0.452.0). The HYG skybox catalog is only ~120k nearby stars and never showed the galactic band. Added galactic_band_stars(7000): faint points rejection-sampled as uniform sphere dirs weighted by a Gaussian in galactic LATITUDE (cluster near the plane), in the SAME equatorial J2000 frame as the catalog (NGP RA 192.86 Dec 27.13; GC Sgr A* RA 266.4 Dec -28.94) so the band falls where it really is and brightens/warms toward the galactic centre. Deterministic xorshift seed (no rand dep), rides the existing star shader (no new pipeline). Cosmetic; pairs with the celestial pass. Compiles native+relay, theme lint ok.

## 2026-06-14

**Decision:** CELESTIAL FAR PASS (v0.450.0) - keystone for the real-scale-universe vision. ## 2026-06-14

**Decision:** FIXED star skybox clipping (v0.446.0, BUG-040). Operator: showroom black void + no stars/orbits/constellations in the roofless home; guessed showroom overrides play. Real root cause: stars.wgsl places stars+constellations at direction*5000, but StarRenderer::update_camera used the GAMEPLAY projection whose far=render_distance (default 500m) -> the whole skybox was beyond the far plane and clipped. Latent forever (roofed home hid it); the showroom + roof-off merely exposed it. Fix: update_camera builds its OWN projection perspective_rh(fov,aspect,1.0,100000) just for the depthless star pass. Stars+constellations now render in home (roof off) + showroom. STILL OPEN: planet (GEO ~42000km) + solar bodies (millions km) + orbit rings (AU) are also clipped by the 500m gameplay far -> need a dedicated celestial far pass; showroom Earth/Mars backdrop should use a LOCAL placeholder sphere near the avatar, not the real distant body.

**Why:** Operator-reported visual bug I could not see; traced statically: star distance 5000 > far 500 = clipped. Verified: native compiles, theme_token_lint passes. The celestial-far pass + construction mode are the next builds.

**Files:** src/renderer/stars.rs, docs/BUGS.md

## 2026-06-13

**Decision:** PIPE WALL-PENETRATION SLEEVES (v0.436.0). Operator wants to keep the engineering-accurate to-code theme; asked for a wall-penetration collar (scientifically motivated - pipes never just pass through a bare wall). Added generically: routing.rs::wall_crossings() samples each routed leg against room AABBs and PipePart::Penetration is emitted at every transition between which room (if any) contains the line (leaving a room into open space OR crossing into an adjacent room both = a wall; same-room runs pierce nothing). Rendered as a steel sleeve (fat short tube along pipe axis) + a wider escutcheon ring. plan_pipe now takes room AABBs; lib.rs builds them from room_info. Unit test: 2 rooms with a gap -> 2 penetrations, same-room -> 0. Verified native+relay compile, 5 routing tests pass.

## 2026-06-13

**Decision:** FIX mouse sensitivity not applied on boot (v0.435.0, BUG-038). Operator: sensitivity super high on spawn until adjusted; shows 0.0. Diagnosed: config.json DID save the value (0.10948) - not a save bug. Two issues: (1) camera controller booted at CameraController::new(5.0,3.0) hardcoded and only synced from settings in the `if settings_dirty` block (fires only on slider move), so every launch used 3.0 (old default, ~12x operator value) until nudged; FOV+render-distance had the same latent boot bug. (2) shows-0.0 was a DISPLAY artifact: slider max 10.0 selects labeled_slider 1-decimal format so 0.109 -> 0.1 with no low-end precision. Fix: set settings_dirty=true right after config load so the apply block pushes loaded fov+sensitivity+fullscreen+render-distance on frame 1; retune default 3.0->0.25 (3 spots); slider range 0.01..=10 -> 0.02..=1.0 (2-decimal display + usable band); guard apply against <=0 (would freeze the look).

**Why:** Operator-reported camera bug. Lesson: a settings_dirty-gated apply block silently never runs on boot, so loaded settings dont reach the engine until the user touches each control. Verified: native+relay compile, all 4 gui lints pass.

**Files:** src/lib.rs, src/config.rs, src/gui/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/settings.rs, docs/BUGS.md


## 2026-06-13

**Decision:** REALISTIC PIPE ROUTING (v0.434.0). Operator (home is on a rotating spaceship ring): pipes were straight diagonal tubes spearing through walls/machines; wants proper plumber/electrician routing with inner/outer diameter, brackets, valves. Grounded the params in a real-world spec via a research agent (ASME A13.1 pipe color, IPC 308.5/NEC 358.30 support spacing, NEC 300.4 power-above-water). Implemented: orthogonal up-over-down routing (riser up, right-angle run along an overhead service band one axis per leg = single 90deg elbows, riser down; no diagonals; degenerate legs collapse; run height clears machines + clamps under the lower of two ceilings for cross-room). Real fittings: new Mesh::tube ROUND primitive (vs old square segment), sphere elbows at corners, fat short COLLARS at machine ports (the diameter-step that reads as hollow pipe), grey BRACKETS at 1.8m code spacing on horizontal runs, red-lever shutoff VALVE on every fluid line. Services stack in vertical lanes (power above water). Data-driven: ALL geometry in data/routing_rules.ron (run height, per-kind lane+radius, bracket spacing, fitting mults, fluid_kinds) so the operator retunes without recompiling. Fleshed out the previously-empty AutoRouter stub in src/systems/construction/routing.rs with the router + PipePart plan + 4 unit tests. Added air/waste colors.

**Why:** Operator wants the home to look like real-life plumbing/electrical (north star: in-game maps to a real buildable thing). The exposed-services ship aesthetic makes code-correct orthogonal overhead runs the AUTHENTIC look, not a compromise. Verified: native+relay compile, 4 routing tests pass, theme_token_lint clean (touched renderer/mesh.rs).

**Files:** src/systems/construction/routing.rs, src/renderer/mesh.rs, src/lib.rs, src/machines.rs, data/routing_rules.ron


## 2026-06-13

**Decision:** INDOOR GARDEN honest all-food design + dense fill (v0.433.0). Operator asked to fill the 34x34x6m garden with aeroponic towers to provide ALL food. Ran a 4-lens design workflow (density/nutrition/staple-calories/grow-light-energy). Verdict (now in docs/design/self-sufficiency.md): LIGHT not floor area is the cap. Free sunlight = ONE canopy, so 1156 m2 ~= 1000 m2 real canopy ~= a ONE-person complete diet, not three; stacking towers under sun just self-shades. Grow-lights to feed 3 indoors = 30-150+ kWh/day (2.5-12x the 12 kWh budget, EROI ~0.005) = breaks the energy loop. So built SUN-LIT: delivers ALL veg+herbs, ~100% protein, all plant vitamins, and via a small aquaponic fish loop CLOSES B12+omega-3 (the gaps no plant fills); beds+mushrooms+fish add ~half calories + ~a fifth fat; outdoor fields carry the rest. New `arrays` data feature (machines.rs all_instances() + lib.rs): a grid of identical machines is ONE RON line, expanded at load (infinite-of-X). Garden now holds 24 variety towers + 2 apothecary + 18 potato beds + 8 grain trays + 10 oilseed beds + 6 mushroom racks + 2 aquaponic tanks (N=staples, S=towers, E=dark mushrooms, support machines on west wall = short pipes). Greenhouse placeholder retired. Food+Energy loop notes rewritten with real numbers.

**Why:** Operators all-food-from-towers instinct collides with physics, and the mission demands the honest answer not a faked 100%. The tradeoff (sun = area-limited single canopy; grow-lights = energetically negative) IS the educational payoff. Verified: native+relay check clean, machines lib test passes (79 instances expand, all connections resolve), ASCII-clean RON.

**Files:** data/machines/home.ron, src/machines.rs, src/lib.rs, docs/design/self-sufficiency.md

## 2026-06-08

**Decision:** v0.413.0 — INLINE ITEM-DETAIL EXPANSION ('the big one' from the operator's inventory batch: 'click an item row to expand in place — picture/3d + full details over rows — instead of a popup/top detail'). Threaded an inline-body renderer through the tree widget: widgets::container_node + tree_list_ex now take `inline: &mut dyn FnMut(&mut Ui, &str)`, and when a selectable LEAF is the selected one they render inline(ui,id) indented directly UNDER that row (the plain tree_list passes a no-op). In src/gui/pages/inventory.rs: (a) new ItemCardActions struct + draw_item_card() helper that renders the expand-in-place item card = colored placeholder image tile (widgets::placeholder_tile + swatch_color, the universal widgets from v0.411) + category badge + details grid (ID/Qty/Category/Subcategory/Weight/Stack/Material/Durability) + description + Eat/Drink/Plant/Use + Equip + Drop compact buttons, recording the chosen action into ItemCardActions; (b) the You&places backpack tree passes an inline closure that looks the item up from an inventory SNAPSHOT (state.inventory_items.clone()) and calls draw_item_card — snapshot so the card never borrows GuiState mid-render; (c) DELETED the old top-of-panel detail block (~100 lines) + its 5 mid-panel action handlers; the item action now applies AFTER the panel closes (where item_acts is readable and the snapshot-borrowing closure is dropped), bridging into the same pending_consume_item/pending_drink_item/pending_plant_seed/equip/drop paths as before. Net: click an item -> its row expands into the card in place; click again -> collapses (selected_slot toggles). VERIFIED: cargo check --features native clean (borrow design held first try); cargo test --lib 398/0; all FOUR gui lints PASS. NEXT v0.414: adopt expandable_row/row_cell in the Mining section (asteroids/manifest/drones grids -> aligned expandable rows) + the You&places place nodes; consider the long-deferred garden PLOT-TYPES arc (soil/sand/pots/trays, infinite-of-X); web Mission-Dashboard mirror.

**Why:** This was the headline UX item the operator flagged as 'the big one' and the natural completion of the inline-expansion theme (garden slots v0.411, then sections v0.412, now items). Implemented by enhancing the EXISTING tree widget with an optional inline-body callback rather than rebuilding the backpack as a flat expandable_row list — that keeps the place hierarchy (You > home > backpack > items) intact while still expanding the right leaf in place. The snapshot-clone of inventory_items is the key borrow trick: the card sets actions into a plain struct (ItemCardActions) that lives OUTSIDE the panel, so the closure only needs the owned snapshot + &mut struct + theme and never touches GuiState during render — which is why it compiled clean on the first try despite the deeply nested closures. Relocating the 5 action handlers to after the panel (vs their old mid-panel spot) was required because the card now sets them LATER in the frame (inside the tree, not at the top); applying post-panel keeps it single-frame, no lag. Reused placeholder_tile + swatch_color so items get the same picture-placeholder treatment as garden slots — one consistent card language across the app.

**Files:** src/gui/widgets/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/inventory.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json


## 2026-06-08

**Decision:** v0.412.0 — COLLAPSIBLE INVENTORY SECTIONS (operator batch item: 'every section collapsible + more defined, with the standard Collapse/Expand/Start-collapsed on ALL nested lists', and the latest-message ask 'add the collapse/expand to the garden section as well'). New widget src/gui/widgets/mod.rs::section_disclosure(ui,theme,id,title,force)->bool: a closure-FREE collapsible section header — paints a triangle (▶ collapsed / ▼ open) as a SHAPE (no font glyph, never tofu), persists open-state per id in egui memory, and honors a global `force` (Some(false)=collapse, Some(true)=expand). Returns the open bool so the caller guards its body with `if section_disclosure(..) { ...body... }` — NO body closure, so the inventory panel's many `action_*`/with_state borrows stay exactly as-is (this is why I didn't reuse the existing closure-form `collapsible_section`). In src/gui/pages/inventory.rs: HOISTED the Collapse-all/Expand-all/Start-collapsed control bar from inside the You&places section to a GLOBAL bar at the top (so its `tree_force` is computed before any section reads it), and wrapped all five sections — Status / Equipment / You&places / Garden / Mining — each in `if widgets::section_disclosure(... tree_force) {`. The same control set now drives the sections AND the nested places-tree + garden tower-groups in one click. Refreshed the stale 'Garden = aligned TABLE' comment to the slot-row reality. VERIFIED: cargo check --features native clean; cargo test --lib 398/0 (no regression); all FOUR gui lints PASS (note: section_disclosure uses theme.text_secondary()/text_primary() — no color literals; the triangle is painted so no glyph lint; my `// ── ──` box-drawing markers are in COMMENTS which emdash_lint doesn't scan). NEXT v0.413: relocate the selected inventory-ITEM detail from the panel TOP to an inline expandable_row (click an item row -> expand in place into a card, same universal widget as the garden slots — operator's flagged 'the big one'); this needs tree_list_ex (the places/backpack tree) to support per-node inline expansion. Then adopt expandable_row/row_cell in Mining (asteroids/manifest/drones grids) + You&places.

**Why:** Closes the remaining items from the operator's inventory-styling batch in one coherent increment. Chose a CLOSURE-FREE disclosure widget (returns bool, caller guards with `if`) specifically to avoid moving ~340 lines of section body (Garden) into a body closure, which would have forced a massive re-indent AND risked the action_*/with_state mutable-borrow plumbing — the closure-free guard keeps every borrow identical and the diff to ~12 lines (the guards + closes). Painted the triangle as geometry rather than a glyph because the egui font's Geometric-Shapes block (▶▼) renders as tofu (icon_glyph_lint would reject it). Hoisting the control bar to the top fixes a latent ordering issue (it previously lived in the You&places section, AFTER Equipment, so a future Equipment use of tree_force wouldn't see it) and gives the operator one global control set, which is what 'on ALL nested lists' asked for. Left the selected-item-detail relocation for v0.413 because it's a deeper tree-widget change (inline node expansion), not a quick guard.

**Files:** src/gui/widgets/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/inventory.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

The slot view (vs the old flat crop table) is what makes 'Plant this tower' legible: you see the fixed slots, which are filled, which are empty/planned, and click any one for the full plant context + actions. ## 2026-06-08

**Decision:** v0.410.0 — TOWER SLOT MODEL + STACKING-BUG FIX (the data layer for the garden slot redesign; operator hit the bug: 'plant this tower' kept stacking, count went 33->66->99). CropInstance gains tower_slot: Option<u32> (serde default); the FarmingSystem tower handler now FILLS FIXED SLOTS instead of appending: for each slot index it (a) skips if a LIVE crop already occupies that (tower_id, slot) — making replant IDEMPOTENT — and (b) despawns any DEAD crop in the slot first so it refills. Threaded tower_slot through the seed-plant + test CropInstance constructions, GuiCrop, and the lib.rs crop sync. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; farming 9/9 incl. NEW tower_replant_fills_slots_idempotently (plant the same tower twice -> still 2 crops not 4; slots 0 and 1 recorded) + the existing creative/survival tower tests still green (slots empty on first plant). This kills the operator's stacking bug and records which slot each crop is in. Despawn-dead-then-refill makes 'Plant again' clear a wiped tower without the player manually removing dead crops. Kept the crop-table UI for this increment (it still works) so the schema + handler change is provable on its own; the slot-row + card view is its own focused increment.

## 2026-06-08

**Decision:** v0.397.0 — TREE COLLAPSE CONTROLS: Collapse-all / Expand-all buttons + a 'Start collapsed' toggle for the inventory + garden nested lists (operator's third ask: 'add collapse/expand all buttons to the nested lists ... and a checkbox for default collapsed so when I first load the lists start collapsed instead of expanded'). WIDGET: new widgets::tree_list_ex(default_open, force) threads two controls through container_node -> the CollapsingState: default_open sets the initial state of branches with no stored state (Start-collapsed passes false); force = Some(bool) overrides EVERY branch open/closed for one frame (set_open), then persists until the next manual toggle. tree_list stays as the (true, None) wrapper, so no other caller changes. INVENTORY: a one-row control bar above the trees (Collapse all | Expand all | Start collapsed) drives BOTH the places tree and the Garden tree; the three tree_list calls became tree_list_ex(tree_default_open, tree_force). PERSISTENCE FINDING: neither GuiState nor SettingsState is actually saved to disk (SettingsState has a manual Default, is runtime-only), and egui's collapse state is also in-memory only -> so to honor 'when I FIRST LOAD start collapsed' across launches without building a settings-persistence layer, I put trees_start_collapsed in GuiState DEFAULTED TRUE: every launch starts collapsed (his wish) for free; he can Expand-all or untoggle for a session. Toggling 'Start collapsed' also force-applies to the already-rendered trees that frame so it feels immediate. VERIFIED: cargo check clean, all FOUR gui lints green. **Why:** Third of the operator's directed asks, completing the batch. Generalized the existing tree widget (tree_list_ex) rather than special-casing the inventory, so collapse control is reusable and other callers are untouched. Defaulted trees_start_collapsed=true because the deeper finding is that NO GUI pref persists to disk today and egui's own collapse state resets on restart, so the only way to satisfy 'start collapsed when I first load' without a new persistence layer is to make collapsed the launch default; the toggle still lets him flip it per session, and force-applying on toggle makes it immediate. A real persisted-settings layer is the proper future home for this + creative_mode.

Absent flag = survival = consume, so every existing farming/crafting test still asserts consumption and passes. Toggle lives at the top of the inventory left panel (a widgets::toggle Creative mode + a one-line hint that flips Creative/Survival), discoverable where the operator is building the garden. ## 2026-06-08

**Decision:** v0.392.0 — TOWER COMPATIBILITY CHECK: "can these plants share one reservoir + air?" (operator’s standing ask from the max-variety reframe: "make sure they’d all grow together too"). Aeroponics shares ONE nutrient reservoir + ONE air volume (not soil), so soil companion/adverse rules relax and the real constraint is a COMMON pH / temperature / humidity window every plant in a tower tolerates. Built it on the ph/temp/humidity data v0.391 just made PlantDef parse: new TowerCompat struct + compute_tower_compat(tower, registry) + an intersect_axis helper (gui/mod.rs) that INTERSECTS each axis across the tower’s distinct species — Some((lo,hi)) if all windows overlap (they can share it), None if empty (a conflict), naming the two binding extremes (highest floor vs lowest ceiling) per conflicting axis. Degenerate 0..0 windows (a missing CSV column) are skipped so absent data can’t fake a conflict; species missing from the registry are skipped. Cached in GuiState.tower_compat (parallel to tower_configs), computed ONCE in the lib.rs crop sync (where plant_reg is already fetched; same disjoint-field borrow as the crop loop; guarded by is_empty so it runs a single time, in the menu loop too). Rendered on the Home page per tower (homes.rs draw_tower, threaded compat through draw_design): green ‘✓ These N plants share one reservoir: pH x-y, a-b°C, humidity p-q%’ when clean, else ‘Shared where they can: …’ + a ⚠ line per conflict (‘Temp: Rosemary vs Lettuce have no overlap’) + a ‘split into a separate tower/zone’ hint. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; new gui::tower_compat_tests 2/2 (compatible plants → one shared window + no conflict; non-overlapping temp → flagged, pH still reported); farming 5/5; all FOUR gui lints green (✓ U+2713 + ⚠ U+26A0 are reliable per CLAUDE.md; no em-dash, hyphen ranges). The real max-variety towers (33 distinct food / 24 herbs) will likely surface genuine temp conflicts — that IS the feature working (the data is real: tomato ph 6.0-6.8, 18-30°C, humidity 0.5-0.8). DEFERRED — NEXT tower features: seed economy (planting a tower should cost seeds, not be free/dev), and the real-world parts list (the north-star real-build bridge). Could also DEEPEN the check: show per-plant which axis pushed it out, or compute the largest compatible SUBSET. NEXT: seed economy or parts list (operator’s pick); else deepen the compat readout.

**Why:** This is the operator’s explicit "grow together" requirement, and v0.391 had just made the needed pH/temp/humidity data available in PlantDef — so it was the natural, ready next feature (the directive is to keep shipping directed work, resolving reversible forks by making the call). Chose the reservoir-intersection model because it is the physically correct constraint for aeroponics (shared water+air, not soil) — the insight the operator himself flagged when reframing to max-variety. Put the compute where the registry already lives (the crop sync) and cached it in GuiState so the Home page (which only gets GuiState) can render it without plumbing the DataStore into the page. Surfaced it on the Home page tower browser because that is the design-reference view; reversible placement, so no pause. Named the binding plants per conflict so the readout is ACTIONABLE (which plants to move), not just a red/green verdict.

**Files:** src/gui/mod.rs, src/lib.rs, src/gui/pages/homes.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

## 2026-06-07

**Decision:** v0.387.0 — FIX: plant-a-tower (v0.386) did nothing (operator: 'nothing happens when I click plant a tower or dev grow all'). ROOT CAUSE: I registered the new 'plant_tower_request' DataStore channel in the WRONG place. The gardening channels are registered in TWO spots: the runtime (lib.rs ~984-990, in the winit `resumed` startup) AND a TEST helper farming::gardening_tests::make_store (farming/mod.rs ~547, 'mirroring the runtime wiring'). My v0.386 edit anchored on `data.insert("plant_request", ...)` with replace_all:false, which matched the FIRST occurrence -- the TEST make_store -- so the channel was registered for the tests but NOT the runtime. At runtime data.get("plant_tower_request") returned None, so the bridge wrote nothing + the FarmingSystem handler drained nothing -> no crops spawned. (dev-grow-all 'did nothing' too simply because there were no crops to grow -- it is gated on existing crops, not broken.) FIX: added `data_store.insert("plant_tower_request", Mutex::new(Option::<Vec<String>>::None))` to the RUNTIME registration in lib.rs (next to plant_request). Verified the rest of the chain is ungated + runs in the menu: system_runner.tick (lib.rs 1646) + the bridge + the GuiState.crops sync are NOT gated on world_loaded (world_loaded only gates the lazy 3D-world LOAD at lib.rs 3676), and the FarmingSystem is registered at startup (lib.rs 1021) -- consistent with the operator's vitals decaying in the menu. So with the channel registered, the full loop now works from the Inventory Garden without entering 3D. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; release build + emdash_lint pending. LESSON (logged): when adding a DataStore channel, register it in the RUNTIME (lib.rs resumed, ~984) AND the test make_store (farming/mod.rs); replace_all:false on a string that exists in both hits the test first. NEXT: operator re-test plant->grow->harvest; then the compatibility check + tower-crop linkage.

**Why:** A real bug from my v0.386 work: the channel-registration anchor matched the test helper before the runtime, so the runtime never knew the channel. Diagnosed by tracing the symptom (both plant-tower AND dev-grow 'do nothing' -> the FarmingSystem isn't getting the command) rather than guessing, which led to the duplicate-registration-site discovery (grep showed the runtime channels live in lib.rs 982-1000, and the farming/mod.rs inserts I'd edited were inside make_store, a #[cfg(test)] helper). Confirmed nothing else is gated on world_loaded so the menu-driven garden works without 3D. Logged the lesson so the next channel addition does not repeat it.

**Files:** src/lib.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

NEXT: the compatibility check (plant pH/temp/humidity shared window); tying tower crops back to their tower (a tower_id on CropInstance so the inventory tower nodes show 'N/M ready'); then the seed-economy + the real-world parts list.

**Why:** The operator said keep developing, and the highest-value next step was making the towers FUNCTIONAL (they were only display so far). Investigating first paid off hugely: the entire gardening loop (growth, water, harvest, the GUI mirror, the Garden render) was reusable, so the hookup was just a new command channel + a batched-spawn handler + a button -- I added almost no new gameplay logic, I connected the towers to the proven loop. Used the dev-friendly no-seed-cost default I had floated to the operator (he repeatedly said 'just get it to work'), keeping the seed economy as a later layer. Put the 'Plant a tower' buttons in the inventory Garden section where crops already live, so the plant->grow->harvest loop is all in one place. Verified the existing farming tests still pass (the full plant-grow-harvest loop) so the new handler didn't regress the gardening system.

## 2026-06-07

**Decision:** v0.384.0 — AEROPONIC TOWERS increment 2b: fix inverted cylinder normals + DATA-DRIVEN tower geometry. Operator (with a screenshot of v0.383): 'face normals are inverted, I'm seeing the inside of the cylinder. At least I can see them! We'll need to design the towers + determine the amount DYNAMICALLY. The helix design is great, scales infinitely. We could allow a wide-diameter tower + adjust helix density vertically, like coarse vs fine threads on a bolt.' FIXES: (1) INVERTED NORMALS: the cylinder side rendered backfacing (you saw the inner far wall) while the SPHERE rendered fine. Root cause: my cylinder used a different (effectively reversed) index winding than the sphere. Fixed by rebuilding Mesh::cylinder with ROW-MAJOR rings (bottom ring then top ring, ring*(seg+1)+i) and the IDENTICAL winding as Mesh::sphere ([a,b,a+1, a+1,b,b+1]) -- now outward-facing. Dropped the top/bottom caps (they were also inverted + a real tower's top is open-ish anyway); it is a solid-walled open tube. (2) DATA-DRIVEN GEOMETRY (his 'dynamic + scalable' + bolt-thread idea): TowerConfig gains diameter_m + height_m + helix_turns (serde defaults 0.4 / 2.0 / 4.0); the RON sets them per tower to SHOW the parametrization -- nutrition = wide + fine (0.6m / 2.4m / 6 turns), apothecary = narrow + coarse (0.32m / 1.9m / 2.5 turns). load_world now reads each tower's geometry: a per-tower cylinder of that diameter/height + one plant-marker sphere per CURATED VARIETY (dynamic count = plantings.len(), capped at 40 for the object budget) along a helix of helix_turns wraps, markers sitting just off the column (radius + 0.12). Towers spaced by their width so wide ones do not overlap. Borrow-safe: geometry snapshotted into a local Vec before the renderer mutations. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; tower test passes (RON + geometry parse, max-variety holds); release build + emdash_lint pending. Visual correctness operator-verified next (the winding fix is reasoned from the working sphere; can't run GUI headless). NEXT: the compatibility check (plant pH/temp/humidity shared window + outlier flags) + the farming hookup. The fuller dynamic model (capacity computed FROM geometry: circumference x height / spacing; plants_per_turn) is a refinement once planting is real.

**Why:** The operator caught a real visual bug (inverted cylinder faces) and gave a strong design direction (dynamic, scalable geometry). The winding fix was diagnosable from the evidence: the sphere rendered correctly, so I made the cylinder use the sphere's exact winding (row-major rings) rather than guessing a flip -- a principled fix, not trial-and-error (which I can't do headless). His coarse-vs-fine-threads framing is a clean parametric model, so I made diameter + height + helix density data-driven per tower and set the two towers to visibly DIFFERENT values so he can confirm the parametrization works at a glance. The plant count follows the curated varieties (his 'one of each' max-variety), with the geometry shaping the arrangement. Kept the deeper capacity-from-geometry math for when planting is real (don't over-build before the farming loop needs it).

## 2026-06-07

**Decision:** v0.381.0 — SAVE/LOAD LIFECYCLE (homes increment 3): offline progress now PERSISTS between sessions. Operator: 'keep developing offline.' A read-only Explore agent mapped the lifecycle; KEY FACTS: (a) the game persisted NOTHING between sessions before this (persistence::{save_world,load_world,auto_save} were wired ONLY in tests; entering the 3D world calls a different EngineState::load_world that regenerates the homestead fresh); (b) system_runner.tick at lib.rs:1554 is UNGATED -- systems run every frame in the menu-driven loops AND in 3D -- so the ECS player entity (spawned once at startup, lib.rs:985-996, with Inventory/PlayerSkills/Health/Vitals/etc.) is authoritative ALWAYS; (c) inventory + skills have clean get/set, while health/position need glam + vitals/crops/quests are NOT in WorldSave. BUILT a new src/save_load.rs: extract_world_save (player INVENTORY + SKILLS -> WorldSave), apply_save_to_world (WorldSave -> player, offline-kind-guarded), load/save_active_home (a single offline_home.json in saves_dir; progressive disclosure = one home), maybe_periodic_save (self-throttling static-timer, every 120s). WIRED 4 hooks in lib.rs: pub mod save_load; APPLY at STARTUP right after the player spawns (NOT on 3D-enter -- because the player is authoritative from startup, and applying-at-startup also makes the exit-save SAFE: the player always carries the loaded state, so closing without playing round-trips the save instead of overwriting it empty); SAVE on WindowEvent::CloseRequested (graceful close); PERIODIC save after the tick (robust to in-app-quit/crash where CloseRequested would not fire). SCOPE = inventory + skills ONLY (the actual progress, lowest coupling -- no Transform/glam); DEFERRED health/position/game_time (TimeSystem owns its clock)/vitals/crops/quests, so reload = 'wake rested at home with your stuff + skills intact'. 2 new tests (extract->wipe->apply round-trips inventory+skills; apply ignores non-offline kind) PASS + persistence round-trip. VERIFIED: cargo check clean (no warnings); 3 save_load/persistence tests pass; release build + emdash_lint pending. NEXT (offline): extend the save to health/position/game_time (game_time needs a TimeSystem set_time), then vitals + crops + quests (each needs a new WorldSave field + a no-double-spawn guard for crops); then the self-sufficiency SCORE data layer once the operator reacts to the variables doc.

**Why:** The operator said keep developing offline, and the real prize was that the game persisted nothing between sessions, so wiring save/load is genuine new value (not polish). Investigating first was essential and paid off: it revealed the tick is ungated (so the ECS player is authoritative from startup, which is why apply-at-startup is correct, not the agent's suggested 3D-enter hook) and it surfaced the data-loss trap (extract-on-close would overwrite a good save with empty if the player never played) -- solved elegantly by apply-at-startup, which makes the player always carry the loaded state so close-save round-trips. Scoped to inventory+skills only to keep this correctness-sensitive first slice clean and low-coupling (no glam, no schema changes), with the riskier fields (crops need a no-double-spawn guard, game_time needs TimeSystem cooperation) deferred to their own careful increments. Added a periodic save because the operator may quit via the in-app menu (not the window X), and losing a session's progress would be a bad first impression. Tested the core round-trip + the kind-guard rather than shipping unverified save logic.

**Files:** src/save_load.rs, src/lib.rs, docs/design/homes-as-profiles.md, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json


## 2026-06-07

**Decision:** v0.380.0 — SELF-SUFFICIENCY model doc + SAVE-WRAPPER model (homes increment 2). Operator asked '(1) what variables are there to consider for homestead self-sufficiency? (2) go ahead and start the save wrapper.' BOTH delivered. (1) NEW docs/design/self-sufficiency.md: a thorough breakdown of the variables, organized as coupled LOOPS (energy / water / food / waste-nutrients / air / thermal-envelope / materials-maintenance), each with supply/demand/storage/losses/time-window, PLUS the cross-cutting gates (location+climate = the single biggest driver, scale/occupancy, autonomy margin, time horizon, loop COUPLING as a network, labor, redundancy). Key honest insights captured: energy is Wh-over-time + storage NOT nameplate watts (the exact reason I refused to ship a naive ratio); self-sufficiency = the MINIMUM across loops (Liebig's limiting factor); the loops are a coupled graph; everything is gated by place + household size. Proposed a buildable SCORE model: per-loop min(1, supply_over_time/demand_over_time) + an autonomy-days number + overall = the limiting loop, gated by location+scale, same metric sim/real (sensors feed it in Real mode). Listed the data we'd add (an editable component-output table: solar W + sun-hours, tank L, etc.) and what's deferred (full network sim, weather modeling). (2) SAVE-WRAPPER MODEL: KEY FINDING from reading the code -- the game has NO working save/load lifecycle today: persistence::{save_world,load_world,auto_save} are defined but wired ONLY in tests; entering the 3D world calls a DIFFERENT EngineState::load_world that REGENERATES the homestead fresh (src/ship/fibonacci::generate_homestead) and never applies a saved state. So 'the save wrapper' splits: the MODEL is mine to build now, the LIFECYCLE (Play loads a home, progress persists) is a careful multi-system increment that the game lacks entirely and deserves its own focus. Built the MODEL: WorldSave gains `kind` (default 'offline') + `design` (default 'fibonacci') via #[serde(default=...)] so pre-v0.380 saves load unchanged; a WorldSave::new_offline(name, design) constructor; 3 tests (new_offline defaults, round-trip preserves kind/design, legacy-JSON-without-the-fields defaults) ALL PASS. The Home page now frames the design as 'your offline home' (a small identity card: kind offline / you own the save / saving+Play-entry is next). Progressive disclosure (#7): one home, no manager, until there's a reason for more. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; 4 persistence lib tests pass; release build + emdash_lint pending. NEXT (offline): increment 3 = the SAVE/LOAD LIFECYCLE -- extract live game state (inventory/skills/game_time/crops/constructions) <-> WorldSave, load the active offline home on world-enter, auto-save on exit/interval (the game currently persists NOTHING between sessions except config/identity, so this is real new value). Then the self-sufficiency SCORE data layer (improvement #4) once the operator reacts to the variables doc + the editable component-output numbers.

**Why:** The operator asked the self-sufficiency question genuinely (he's unsure how he thinks about it), so the most useful thing was a thorough, organized variable breakdown he can react to -- persisted to a design doc because it's durable knowledge that shapes the score feature + the whole real-buildable north star, not a throwaway reply. I led with the honest engineering truth (energy is Wh+storage not nameplate; Liebig's minimum) because correctness matters more than a flashy number, and proposed a concrete buildable model so we're not stuck in abstraction. For the save wrapper, reading the code first paid off: the game has no save/load at all, so I scoped honestly -- ship the clean low-risk MODEL now (kind+design + backward-compat + tests), and treat the lifecycle as its own careful increment rather than rushing a multi-system save/load into an already-large turn (correctness not sacrificed for speed). Used #[serde(default)] so this is a zero-migration change. Kept the Home page to a single-home framing (progressive disclosure, improvement #7) rather than building a multi-home manager nobody needs offline yet.

**Decision:** v0.377.0 — PLAY button (FPS-mode entry) + HOMES-AS-PROFILES direction adopted. (1) PLAY BUTTON shipped (operator: 'add a dedicated button for the FPS game part ... right now it's just I press Esc to bring up the FPS game mode, there's no indicator in the menu ... Click Play to start FPS game mode'). Mechanism: FPS mode IS GuiPage::None (the nav bar + pages are hidden for None/MainMenu per lib.rs ~3650; the post-egui reconcile ~3929 grabs the cursor when a frame ends on None). So 'Play' is a nav button whose page = GuiPage::None — clicking it hides the chrome and grabs the mouse for look, exactly like pressing Esc from a page. Added paint_play (right-pointing filled triangle) in icons.rs + routed P::None -> paint_play; placed Play to LEAD the game-colored cluster (Play · Quests · Inventory · Crafting); and tweaked the generic nav click handler so entering None records last_page = the page you came from (Esc out of the world returns there, not to a stale last_page). Nav is now 11: Humanity, Chat, Studio, Real, Play, Quests, Inventory, Crafting, Platform, Library, Settings (slightly over the <=10 guide, acceptable since Play is an action that hides the nav). (2) HOMES-AS-PROFILES MODEL ADOPTED (operator's bigger proposal, captured in NEW docs/design/homes-as-profiles.md): each HOME is a SAVE PROFILE rendered by ONE shared homestead interface, differing only by a 'kind' toggle — Offline (local sim; the FIRST offline home = the 100%-self-sustaining Fibonacci design = the gamified blueprint others copy), Server (multiplayer on a relay), or Real (bound to real monitoring/automation hardware; the north-star control layer, built LAST). Homes are built from DESIGNS (blueprints; first = Fibonacci spiral-deck homestead). This DISSOLVES the Real/Play firewall: real-vs-game becomes a property of the home you're in, not a top-level page split — the same UI, different connection. Play (this increment) enters the world for the SELECTED home. The doc maps it to existing code (saves/persistence, the Place spine, ship/RON layouts + the Fibonacci generator, relay multiplayer, device-mesh) and sequences it: Play DONE -> home model+select -> offline Fibonacci design -> server homes -> parts-list-from-design -> real homes LAST. VERIFIED: cargo check clean; release build + emdash_lint pending (in flight). NOTE: did NOT build the save-model changes — that is a real architecture needing operator alignment on the open forks in the doc (can a home change kind? design-vs-home split? where home-select lives? what a Real home shows); recorded them rather than guessing.

**Why:** The Play button is a small, concrete, decided win that fixes a real discoverability gap (no on-screen way into FPS mode) and reuses the existing None=FPS mechanism, so it was pure UI wiring — shipped immediately. The homes-as-profiles model is the operator's synthesis and it is genuinely better than the Real/Play page split we'd been circling: it makes the real-world-bridge north star concrete (design once -> game level + parts list + real dashboard, one interface) and unifies offline/server/real under one homestead UI. Captured it durably in its own design doc the moment it was established (cross-session-persistence rule) with the model, the code mapping, and the open forks — but did NOT speculatively build the save-system rework, because the forks are the operator's architecture call and guessing a big persistence change wrong would waste real work. Built the decided part, documented the rest, kept moving.

## 2026-06-06

**Decision:** DIRECTION SHIFT + REAL-WORLD-BRIDGE NORTH STAR (operator, design discussion). (1) REMOVE the Real/Play distinction: make the survival/production game systems (garden, inventory, crafting, market, etc.) first-class top-level features that just WORK, not wrapped in a real-vs-sim split. Add Crafting to the main menu (top-level). (2) DEFER real-life integration to LAST, but keep it as a design-shaping north star throughout. THE NORTH STAR: every in-game system (garden, water, energy, crafting) should be designed to MAP to a real-world system a person can actually build; that mapping generates a PARTS LIST of everything anyone needs to 3D-print / buy / trade to build these systems at their own home; and LAST, the app gains a way to AUTOMATE + MONITOR those real systems (the app becomes the control/monitoring layer for your real homestead, e.g. real aeroponics at the operator's house). Design the game systems NOW as real buildable systems, not just game abstractions, so this is achievable later. (3) This SUPERSEDES the earlier 'Real vs Sim = separate pages, never a toggle' firewall framing FOR NOW: the operator is collapsing it to build the systems first; any real/sim separation + the real-life layer return LAST. (4) REORG PENDING: the operator is unsatisfied with the cramped Real page (Profile sections + Inventory/Wallet/Tasks/Map/Market all crammed in one) and explicitly asked for my thoughts on how to reorganize. I am proposing a homestead-centered IA, Profile (you) | Home (your homestead: possessions/garden/market/wallet/tasks/map) | Crafting (make/3D-print), removing Real + Play, and asking him to pick the granularity before I build.

**Why:** The operator is reprioritizing: get the survival/production systems working as first-class top-level features now, drop the real/sim wrapper that added friction, and treat the real-life-automation layer as the LAST step, but one that shapes every system's design (each must map to a real buildable thing + a parts list). Recorded the real-world bridge as a durable north star because he explicitly said to 'keep it in mind while we develop'; it is the project's deepest purpose (teach + equip real self-sufficiency, then automate it) and must survive a compaction. Asked before reorganizing because he said he is unsure how and asked for thoughts: a genuine information-architecture fork in his design domain, where guessing a big nav rebuild wrong would waste real work.

The liberty half of the same promise: ending poverty is not enough if the result is a cage. VERIFIED: cargo check clean, release build clean, emdash_lint passes, quests.json valid + universal (no Lake Tahoe / nation stats).

**Why:** Both came from the operator reading the live build. (1) The Lake Tahoe line was exactly the kind of unverifiable, place-specific claim that undermines trust (and excludes the billions who do not live near it); universalizing the quests, deferring specifics to Resources links, makes each one read as the user's own regardless of climate or economy, which is the mission's reach. Fixed in the single data file both clients load, so native and web stay consistent for free. (2) The page argued the poverty case (v0.366) but said nothing about the freedoms a free people needs; the operator flagged free speech as paramount, so I added the liberty dimension in his own words and showed it is defended BY DESIGN (the architecture), not promised on top. This continues the app-first loop: more concrete detail, consistent voice, both the material and the civic stakes made plain.

**Files:** data/onboarding/quests.json, src/gui/pages/humanity.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

## 2026-06-05

**Decision:** v0.364.0 — WHOLE-APP EM-DASH SWEEP + a regression lint (operator: 'go through the whole app and assess for em dashes', extending the v0.363 ban from the Humanity page to EVERYTHING). Swept every user-facing surface: (1) NATIVE src/gui = 121 string em-dashes across 13 files via scripts/strip-emdash-strings.js (a dotall string-literal regex catching single AND multi-line literals, leaving comments alone); fixed 2 cosmos placeholders the first pass mangled (orbits-fallback ', ' to '-'; the '— upcoming —' divider to 'Upcoming'). (2) WEB = 1048 across 94 files via scripts/strip-emdash-web.js (global, since HTML text is not quoted; spaced prose to ', ', the rest to '-'). REVERTED two files it touched that it must NOT: the VENDORED noble-pq.bundle.js and the GENERATED theme.css. REVIEWED the crypto-file diffs (crypto.js, pq.js) line-by-line: every change is a comment or a user-facing message, ZERO functional strings (no signed-preimage separator, KDF context, or compared value touched), and a global replace keeps intra-web comparisons consistent on both sides. The excluded crypto libs (pq-identity/pq-object/pq-relay-auth/canonical-cbor/bip39) retain em-dashes ONLY in comments (verified). (3) DATA = 328 across 31 files via scripts/strip-emdash-data.js (per-format: JSON/RON/TOML get ', '/'-' since commas are safe inside their quoted values; CSV gets ' - ' because a comma is a column DELIMITER and would corrupt the row). JSON validated 46/46 parse-OK. EXCLUDED intentionally: data/coordination/** (internal journal/sessions), *.md (dev docs), and announcements_archive.json + legacy_channel_content.json (HISTORICAL message records, rewriting them would edit the past). src/relay was NOT blanket-swept (643 occurrences, overwhelmingly backend comments/SQL, not user-facing, and risky). GUARD: tests/emdash_lint.rs is a cargo test that scans src/gui string literals via a string-vs-comment state machine (with a // emdash-exempt hatch) and FAILS the build on any new string em-dash; a self-verifying unit test proves the scanner flags strings AND ignores comments (not a no-op). It is the theme_token_lint / icon_glyph_lint analog for the em-dash ban. VERIFIED: release build clean (v0.364.0 exe), cargo test --release --test emdash_lint = 2/2 pass, grep confirms only the intended exclusions retain em-dashes on every surface. ENV NOTE: linking the DEBUG bin hits MSVC 'LNK1318 Unexpected PDB error; LIMIT' (the debug PDB is too big for this project); run cargo tests via --release (reuses the release artifacts) as the workaround. The release build and CI are unaffected.

**Why:** Operator directive to sweep the WHOLE app, not just the landing. Did it as one comprehensive ship across all three user-facing surfaces (native/web/data) with per-format CARE rather than a blind global replace, because correctness was the real constraint: the CSV comma-as-delimiter trap, the crypto-string safety review, reverting the vendored+generated files, and refusing to rewrite historical message archives are each a place a careless sweep would have broken something. Added the lint because a sweep without a guard silently regresses (the no-bandaids rule): the next edit that adds a user-facing em-dash now fails the build, the same way hardcoded colors and tofu glyphs do. Left code comments + dev docs + src/relay alone deliberately, none are rendered to users and churning 600+ backend comments adds risk for zero user benefit. The web is now em-dash-clean too, which directly helps the logged web-landing mirror (it inherits a clean base).

**Files:** scripts/strip-emdash-strings.js, scripts/strip-emdash-web.js, scripts/strip-emdash-data.js, tests/emdash_lint.rs, src/gui (13 files), web (94 files), data (31 files), src/gui/pages/cosmos.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

Captured the mission spec to a design doc IMMEDIATELY (cross-session rule — durable knowledge hits disk the moment it's given) because it's the project's PURPOSE definition + the demo-persona rationale + the AI-inclusion principle, none of which can survive a compaction otherwise. Kept profile::draw for the legacy dispatch so nothing breaks while the fold is partial.

## 2026-06-02

**Decision:** v0.356.0 — SEED-PHRASE REVEAL now PASSPHRASE-GATED (extended the lockable_gate to the real crown jewel — after catching + correcting a WRONG target). I'd told the operator I'd lock Recovery + Identity per their 'crypto coin and other private data sections,' but VERIFIED them first and found neither is actually private: Identity is a PUBLIC did:hum lookup tool (look up ANY DID's public key / trust / VCs — all public data), Recovery is SOCIAL key-recovery SETUP (guardian + Shamir config, NOT the seed). Locking the public Identity lookup would have been a real mistake. The genuinely-sensitive data is the 24-word SEED PHRASE in Settings → 'Identity & Seed Phrase', which previously revealed on a single 'Show Seed Phrase' click with NO passphrase — a real gap (anyone at an unlocked, unattended screen could reveal the account master key). FIX: the seed reveal now runs through widgets::lockable_gate('Reveal seed phrase', verify = decrypt_private_key(enc, salt, pass, iters).is_ok()) — re-enter the vault passphrase to show the words; Lock/restart re-hides. No-vault fallback (a freshly-generated seed not yet encrypted) keeps the plain show/hide so a brand-new user can still write down their words before setting a passphrase. VERIFIED: cargo check --features native clean + 386/386 native lib tests. LESSON (re-affirmed): verify WHICH data is private before locking it — 'private sections' is a judgment about the DATA, and I nearly auto-locked a public tool; reading the pages caught it. Remaining genuinely-private candidate = the Profile PRIVATE group (Body & Measurements, Private Notes) — a finer per-section integration AND partly the operator's call on what they consider private, so left for their steer rather than auto-applied.

**Why:** Keep-shipping the 'other private data sections' ask — but correctness FIRST: I read Recovery + Identity instead of blindly wrapping them, and they're NOT private (one is a public lookup), so locking them would have been wrong + user-hostile. Redirected to the actual crown jewel — the seed phrase — which had a genuine one-click-reveal gap that the operator's exact pattern (passphrase to reveal private data) closes. Reused decrypt_private_key (real vault auth) so the gate truly verifies, not security theatre. Kept the no-vault fallback so a brand-new user can still record their seed before they've set a passphrase. Did NOT auto-lock the Profile private fields because WHICH personal data counts as 'private' is the operator's judgment (I just demonstrated the cost of guessing) — surfacing it for their steer instead of guessing again.
