## 2026-06-02

**Decision:** v0.355.0 — LOCKABLE PRIVATE SECTIONS (operator spec: 'The crypto coin and other private data sections that should always be locked when not actively in use could always be collapsed and require the passphrase to open/expand. The bar with the title... <title><show/hide><unlock><text entry box for passphrase fills the rest>'). NEW universal widget widgets::lockable_gate(ui, theme, lock:&mut LockState, title, verify: impl Fn(&str)->bool) -> bool + widgets::LockState{unlocked,input,show,error}: a private-section gate, collapsed+LOCKED by default; the caller renders the body ONLY when it returns true. Locked header = exactly the operator's layout — [Title] [Show/Hide (passphrase reveal toggle)] [Unlock] [passphrase TextEdit fills the rest, masked]. Unlocked header = [Title] … [Lock] (Lock = collapse = re-lock, the 'locked when not in use' model). DECOUPLED via a verify CLOSURE — the widget never handles the secret beyond the typed input + does no crypto itself, so it's truly universal (any section supplies its own check). SECURITY: LockState lives in GuiState.section_locks (HashMap<id,LockState>) IN MEMORY ONLY — never persisted, so an app restart re-locks everything; the input clears on unlock/Lock. DEMO + first real use: the Wallet page now gates ALL its content (balance/address/send/history) behind the lock — verify re-runs config::decrypt_private_key(encrypted_private_key, key_salt, typed_pass, key_iterations).is_ok() (the SAME 600k-PBKDF2 + AES-GCM auth that unlocks the seed vault; a wrong passphrase fails AES-GCM auth → Err → stays locked). No-vault fallback (fresh/imported key, empty blob) shows open. All labels plain text (no tofu-risk glyphs); masking via TextEdit::password(!show). VERIFIED: cargo check --features native clean + 386/386 native lib tests. NEXT: apply the same gate to Identity + Recovery + private Profile fields (≈one line each); auto-relock on page-leave / idle is a tracked v2 refinement (manual Lock = collapse already covers 'not in use' per the operator's literal 'collapsed = locked' framing).

**Why:** Operator gave a precise widget spec for a real security need (crypto/identity/recovery locked when idle) — built it exactly, as a universal widget (verify-closure decoupling, like section_nav) so every private section opts in with one call. Real verification against the actual vault (decrypt_private_key) not a fake/visual lock — a lock that doesn't truly verify is security theatre, worse than none. In-memory-only state (never persisted) so a restart always re-locks — the correct posture for secrets. Manual Lock = collapse matches the operator's literal 'collapsed and require the passphrase' (the body isn't even rendered while locked, so it can't leak); the idle-timer auto-relock I'd floated is a refinement, deferred since collapse already gives 'locked when not in use'. Demoed on the Wallet (the operator's named 'crypto coin' target) so it's proven end-to-end, not an unused widget.

**Files:** src/gui/widgets/mod.rs, src/gui/mod.rs, src/gui/pages/wallet.rs, docs/PRIORITIES.md, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json

Falls back to the flat backpack list when place_root is None. DELIBERATELY NOT EMBEDDED in the binary: the seed is the operator's PERSONAL data, not a universal default — distributed builds correctly fall back to flat until a user creates their own places in-app; shipping the operator's Silverdale home as everyone's default would be wrong. Built data-driven (infinite-of-X: the hierarchy is JSON, not hardcoded) so the model leads and the operator edits it next. ## 2026-06-02

**Decision:** v0.352.0 — CHAT COMPOSER FIX (operator bug from live play, with screenshot): an incoming '… is typing' indicator pushed the message text-entry box DOWN below the window's bottom edge / behind the Windows taskbar, even in snapped-fullscreen. ROOT CAUSE (chat.rs ~2272): the input bar is allocated at a FIXED-TOP rect (input_rect.top = available.max.y - input_height) and the reply banner + typing indicator render ABOVE the composer INSIDE that rect. input_height reserved space for the reply banner (reply_banner_h = 22 when replying) but NOT for the typing row — so an incoming typing event consumed ~22px of the fixed input_height and slid the composer down past available.max.y (the window bottom; behind the taskbar in snapped-fullscreen). FIX: mirror the reply_banner_h pattern — compute typing_active (any chat_typing_users entry within the 3s TYPING_TTL, matching the renderer's prune-then-show condition) and add typing_h (22.0) to input_height. Now an incoming typing event grows the input bar UPWARD (the message scroll area shrinks by 22px) and the composer stays anchored at the bottom, exactly where it sits with no typing. Reply + typing can stack (input_height = 52 + 22 + 22). VERIFIED cargo check --features native clean + 386/386 native lib tests. NOTE: the freshness check at the input_height site duplicates the 3s TTL the renderer uses ~900 lines below; left as a mirrored literal (TYPING_TTL is local to the render block) with an explaining comment rather than hoisting a shared const for a one-line dup.

**Why:** Clear, reproducible, screenshot-backed operator bug — fix immediately. The composer being shoved under the taskbar makes chat unusable the instant anyone types, which is exactly mid-conversation. Root cause was a single un-reserved row height (the typing indicator), so the fix is surgical and mirrors the already-correct reply_banner_h reservation — no layout restructure, lowest-risk change. Reserved a slightly generous 22px (same as the reply banner) so the composer can never be cut even if the typing row's true height drifts. Matched the renderer's exact show-condition (fresh within 3s) so the reservation and the drawn row stay in lockstep frame to frame.

**Files:** src/gui/pages/chat.rs, data/coordination/orchestrator_state.json


## 2026-06-02

**Decision:** v0.351.0 — section_nav UNIVERSAL WIDGET (directly answers the operator's question 'Is the section sidebar a simplified universal widget that can easily be applied to any page?' — yes, by making it one + proving it). NEW widgets::SectionNavItem + widgets::section_nav(ui, theme, title, items, active) -> Option<clicked_id>: the generalisation of the Profile page's grouped switcher sidebar. An item carries id (returned on click) + label + accent colour (active-row tint + group-header dot) + an optional group header (set on the first item of each group). The widget renders an optional title, a group header wherever a group opens (accent dot + uppercase label), and each row in the Profile active-highlight style (white text + accent-alpha-30 fill + accent-alpha-100 stroke; the alpha tints are computed from the caller's accent, so NO hardcoded palette in the widget). The CALLER owns the active-id state and decides what a click DOES — switch the shown section OR scroll a long page to that section's anchor — so the SAME widget serves a switcher page and an infinite-scroll TOC alike (covers the operator's 'left side panel ... navigable table of contents for quickly navigating huge pages'). PROVED universal by REFACTORING the Profile page onto it: deleted profile.rs's local section_header + sidebar_item helpers, replaced the hand-built sidebar with a SectionNavItem list + one section_nav call + a ProfileSection<->string-id mapping (section_id/section_from_id); identical look + grouped-switcher behaviour, now DRY. VERIFIED: cargo check --features native clean + 386/386 native lib tests. This is STEP 2 of the merge-pages arc (after v0.349 tree_list): the two foundational universal widgets — tree_list (nested containers) + section_nav (page TOC) — are now BOTH in place, so the merged Real/Play pages can be assembled from collapsible sections + a section_nav TOC + tree_list inventories. STILL OPEN in the arc: reconcile the TWO tree widgets into one (migrate the Files page off the closure-based widgets/tree.rs onto tree_list, retire the closure one); THEN the Real/Play/Platform page split (await the operator's bucket-mapping nod).

**Why:** The operator explicitly ASKED whether the section sidebar could be a universal widget — the best possible answer is to build it as one and prove it on a real page, not describe it. Generalised Profile's EXISTING pattern (the operator said 'extend the Profile page's section sidebar') rather than inventing a new nav. Kept the widget click-action-AGNOSTIC (returns the clicked id; the caller switches or scrolls) so the single widget covers BOTH the switcher pages that exist today AND the infinite-scroll TOC the merged pages want — no design fork to resolve, no rework when a merged page wants scroll-to. Refactored Profile onto it in the SAME increment (not shipping an unused widget) — that DRYs the duplicate helpers AND is the proof-of-universality the operator's question deserves. Bucket-independent, so safe to ship before the Real/Play confirmation; keeps the keep-shipping momentum on foundational work while the page-bucketing (the operator's call) stays pending.

## 2026-06-12

**Decision:** SECURITY SPRINT started (operator chose it over First Playable / plot-types). Operator decided the signing scheme via AskUserQuestion: HYBRID Ed25519 + Dilithium3 (both must verify) + passphrase-encrypted key file signed LOCALLY (never CI). Rationale captured for them: signatures don't have the harvest-now-decrypt-later urgency of encryption, but since Dilithium3 is already in-repo, hybrid gives classical + PQ robustness for the supply-chain root of trust at near-zero marginal cost; key in CI is rejected (defeats the purpose). SHIPPED the CRITICAL (auto-update RCE) across v0.418.0 + v0.419.0: new src/release_update.rs (hybrid sign/verify over a release manifest + keygen + Argon2id/AES-256-GCM encrypted key vault; 10 tests; smoke-tested incl. wrong-passphrase reject + the vault encrypt->decrypt round-trip); src/updater.rs verifies the signed manifest + artifact SHA-256 before installing AND only offers releases carrying a signed manifest (stray/unsigned tags invisible to auto-update); src/main.rs::find_newer_exe verifies a candidate's .sig.json sidecar before launching (closes the local-exec HIGH); CLI --gen-release-key/--sign-release/--sign-file; scripts/make-release-manifest.js + archive-build.js opt-in signing; just gen-release-key/sign-release; docs/release-signing.md. Until provisioned, embedded pubkeys are empty -> updater warns + legacy behaviour (nothing breaks). **ACTIVATION is operator-only + pending: `export HUMANITY_SIGNING_PASSPHRASE=... && just gen-release-key`, commit data/release/signing_pubkeys.json, ship a release, then `just sign-release vX` per release.** The CRITICAL is code-complete but NOT live-closed until that runs. STILL OPEN in the sprint (no operator input needed for most): (b) vault-sync replay nonce [protocol change: web pq-relay-auth.js + native + relay], (c) /api/v2/objects auth + per-author quota, (d) deploy-pipeline signed-tag/approval (interacts with the signed-release flow), (e) member-directory opt-out [needs a default-public-vs-opt-out product call], (f) message retention + bot/announce rate-limit + federation gossip amplification.

**Why:** The updater is the single point that owns every desktop user, so it was the right first target + a launch blocker. Built it fully (remote updater path + local launcher) with the operator's chosen hybrid scheme, but the activation needs their passphrase/key -- a genuine operator-only step + the point at which the CRITICAL actually takes effect, so it's the natural sync. Releases v0.418/v0.419 deploy green; the relay was unaffected (native-only changes) but the relay build was verified each time per the v0.416 lesson.

## 2026-06-18

**Decision:** SHIPPED v0.487.0 -- mic test now accepts any device format+rate (operator screenshot: Failed: does not support 48 kHz f32, status flickering). Root causes: (1) the audio path hardcoded 48 kHz f32; real WASAPI shared-mode mics are commonly 48 kHz i16 or 44.1 kHz. voice.rs now reads default_input_config/default_output_config, builds streams generic over the sample type (i16/u16/f32 via cpal from_sample), and resamples device-rate<->48 kHz with a streaming linear Resampler (exact passthrough at 48 kHz). (2) the toggle re-tried a failing start every frame, flickering Starting/Failed; lib.rs now starts/stops only on the toggle EDGE (GuiState.mic_test_prev) and flips the toggle off if the start fails so the Failed reason stays readable.

**Why:** Operator could not test the mic at all -- their device is not 48 kHz f32, and the failure flickered too fast to read.

Proven by spike_synthetic_click_registers + the REAL inventory_container_header_click_toggles_open. Building it CAUGHT a real fix: a re-interact()ed row needs a STABLE Id for the click to attribute (inventory header now uses ui.interact(rect, Id::new(('place_header',path)), ...)); and a full-width click target's rect.center() can be off-screen. Pattern documented in docs/design/ui-system.md. (2) engine_wiring_lint was RED+unused from a false positive (leading-ident read 'crate' from a path-qualified register(crate::..::SolarSystem::new()) and missed it); fixed registered_systems() to take the final type segment, removed ElectricalSystem from DEFERRED (it is registered), now green + in `just lints` + verify.yml. (3) .github/workflows/verify.yml -- the FIRST CI verification (deploy.yml only built): clean ubuntu runs relay check + 5 standalone lints + doc-links on push/PR (the backstop for the 25-release-red class). (4) Justfile: _commit uses git commit -F (not -m, the PS quote foot-gun); fmt is a hard-stop (banned, Incident v0.390); new `just brief`. (5) scripts/brief.js -- one-shot orient (version drift / last CI / signing / newest journal); it already surfaced LOCAL-AHEAD drift + UNSIGNED latest releases. (6) scripts/agent-status.js staleness banner from each file's audited_at (NOT mtime, which a fresh clone resets -- the data is 57d stale). (7) `just install-hooks` -> node scripts/install-git-hooks.js (the old shebang recipe needed cygpath, absent on Windows, so it silently did nothing); pre-commit dead-path+fmt-blast+relay+lints, pre-push untracked-source; NOT auto-installed (an AI should not wire its own auto-run commands -- left for the operator). Each shipped native+relay green, 469 lib tests (2 new interaction), 5 lints, 0 broken doc links.

**Why:** Operator asked to invest in making development itself easier for every future session (AI + human). (D) offset reach was hardcoded +/-40m / 0..10m so big rooms (144m hangar) were unreachable + machines clipped low ceilings -> now derived from the selected room's real dimensions. (E) unique_instance_id ignored array-expanded ids (latent collision) -> now checks all_instances(). 4 new unit tests + existing suite green; native+relay+lints green; exe archived. The 6th finding (no save-success toast/dirty-guard) is UX polish, consistent with the sibling Save-layout button -- tracked, not blocking.

It paid off -- 5 real bugs in code I'd shipped, including the HashMap-save-churn (C) that would have spammed the operator with meaningless git diffs on every save (exactly the churn they dislike). Put prune logic in testable MachineHome methods reusable by both the editor AND the AI, not inline GUI code. Verified builds+tests+lints before shipping per the no-sacrificing-correctness-for-speed directive.

## 2026-06-23

**Decision:** HOME-DESIGN Stage 3a (buildability validator: power + wiring) SHIPPED (v0.524.0) -- the mission core made computable. MachineHome::buildability_report(sun_hours) is a pure, world-free check over the placed machines (so it runs in the editor AND an AI can call it before committing a design): (1) Power source -- is there a panel/generator for the load; (2) Energy balance -- real kWh/day (solar peak x sun_hours + generators x24h) vs consumption x24h, plus does the battery carry the solar-off window: Pass / Warn (covers day not night) / Fail (can't meet daily demand); (3) Wiring -- every connection endpoint resolves (catches an AI hand-edit dangling ref). Returns BuildabilityReport{checks:[{name,status,detail}]} + worst() verdict. New types CheckStatus + BuildabilityCheck + BuildabilityReport. The construction editor gains a whole-home 'Buildability' section (always shown): each check as a colored verdict (green check / amber warn / red !) + the real numbers. Seed home reads ALL-PASS (3200W panels, 18 vs 1.2 kWh/day, 20 connections valid). VERIFIED: 5 unit tests (load-without-source fails, balanced passes, undersized-battery warns, dangling-connection fails, seed sane) + the construction snapshot re-rendered (switched to the study room so the panel is READABLE -> Machines + Connections + Buildability all render). 13 machines tests + native + relay + 3 lints green; exe building.

**Why:** Continued the home-design arc to its next fully-self-verifiable increment. Stage 3a (power + wiring) is the slice computable from home.ron TODAY -- it reuses the same electrical numbers the live ElectricalSystem uses but as a static design-time check (no world needed), which is exactly what makes an AI design trustworthy + a player design honest (the home-design.md litmus). Stopped Stage 3 at 3a deliberately: 3b (water/structure/materials) needs structured numbers the data doesn't carry yet (machine stats are display strings not L/day; no material_type on machines; the solver isn't wired to rooms) -- that's a data-model step wanting an operator scope call, not a clean check. ## 2026-06-24

**Decision:** INCIDENT + FIX (v0.528.0): the v0.525 live-machine refactor made ALL machines VANISH in a fully-built home -- operator caught it on launch ('All the machines seem to have disappeared. The plumbing/cables is still present'). ROOT CAUSE: the renderer has a hard 256-object-per-frame cap (renderer/mod.rs, `if i >= 256 break`, 8 loops; the MAX_OBJECTS const was LOCAL to the constructor so the draw loops hardcoded the literal). Through v0.524 machines lived INSIDE placeholder_objects (interleaved early, within 256). v0.525 moved them to their own machine_objects list pushed AFTER the whole placeholder list, so with the dense indoor garden (~104 machine meshes = 38 explicit + 66 array towers) + pipes + markers + walls, the machines landed past index 256 and were silently truncated; pipes survived because they sort earlier. FIX: MAX_OBJECTS 256->1024, promoted to a shared module const used by the buffer + all 8 caps (256-byte align x 1024 = 256 KB; the cap is a ceiling so cost stays proportional to actual objects). SECOND BUG fixed same release: rebuild_machine_objects re-created ~104 meshes EVERY call, and an offset drag fires it every frame -> thousands of leaked meshes/sec; now when the machine COUNT is unchanged it reuses meshes + only updates positions (rebuild only on add/remove), plus a guard to not wipe machines if room geometry is momentarily empty. native+relay+16 machines tests+3 lints green; exe building. Result: machines render again, move live with offset edits, and follow a room drag. Pipes still don't follow a room move live (known follow-up).

**Why:** This is exactly the launch-verify-only risk I had flagged about the v0.525 render refactor (can't headlessly snapshot a 3D scene) -- and it bit: I shipped v0.525-0.527 on top of an unconfirmed render change, and the operator's first real test found the machines gone. LESSON: a render-list reorder interacts with the 256-object draw cap; any feature that adds many world objects must account for it (the cap is now 1024 + a named const, so it's visible). Diagnosed by READING the renderer (found the cap + the leak) rather than guessing, then fixed both the truncation and the per-frame mesh leak in one release since both stem from the same v0.525 refactor. Prioritized this as a hotfix over building build-mode step 2 -- a visible-machines editor is the prerequisite for everything else.

**Files:** src/renderer/mod.rs, src/lib.rs

## 2026-06-24

**Decision:** PLUMBING step 1 -- LIVE CONNECTION LINES SHIPPED (v0.530.0). Operator confirmed ghost placement works + said proceed (to easy plumbing). ## 2026-06-24

**Decision:** ADVERSARIAL REVIEW of build-mode (v0.527-0.530) -> FIXED the real bugs (v0.531.0). Ran a 4-dimension review workflow (14 agents, find->verify) while the operator tested v0.530; it confirmed 8 bugs. FIXED: (HIGH) room-drag GPU leak -- apply_room_drag sets construction_dirty every frame -> rebuild_homestead -> apply_homestead_meshes add_mesh+add_material'd ~15-20 buffers/frame and the renderer was APPEND-ONLY (no free path), so a multi-second drag orphaned hundreds-thousands of GPU buffers for the process lifetime. Added a renderer reuse API (replace_mesh: drops old mesh -> wgpu frees, reuses slot; update_material_typed/full: rewrites the existing uniform buffer in place, zero alloc) + made apply_homestead_meshes REUSE its prior slots. (MED) same-root per-edit leaks: rebuild_machine_objects slow path now reuses slots (a single add/remove no longer orphans the whole ~100-mesh home); the ghost reuses its slot on a held-type switch. (MED) stale held-item -- closing build mode (B OR the Close button) left construction_place_type set, so reopen+click silently DROPPED a machine; both close paths now clear it. native+relay+16 tests+3 lints+snapshot green; exe building. DEFERRED follow-ups (latent/cosmetic, in PRIORITIES): 1024 object cap can still be exceeded by a very dense garden (it truncates the hologram not the machines -- needs reorder+warn); sphere ghost not floor-lifted (dormant, no sphere in catalog); ghost previews over panels.

**Why:** Used Ultracode (review workflow) while the operator tested v0.530 + decided the line-look -- a non-preempting, correctness-first use of the wait, the same pattern that paid off on the v0.522 machine-editing review. It paid off again: the HIGH room-drag leak is exactly the v0.527-class per-frame GPU leak (forbidden by the repo rule) but on the homestead-shell path, masked because the machines take their fast path on a room move (placements.len() unchanged) so nothing visibly flickered -- I'd never have caught it by launch-testing. The real root (renderer append-only, no free path) now has a reuse API that ALL the cached-handle rebuilders (shell, machines, ghost) use. Deferred the latent/cosmetic findings to keep the fix release focused on what bites the operator now (leaks while they drag rooms + the wrong-context placement on reopen).

**Files:** src/renderer/mod.rs, src/lib.rs, src/gui/pages/construction.rs


## 2026-06-24

**Decision:** HOME-CONSTRUCTION REDESIGN confirmed by operator + Stage 1 SHIPPED (v0.532.0). The operator hit the wall: rooms-as-sliding-AABBs is the root problem (rooms aren't boxes, they're the space enclosed by walls); the straight-line pipes pass through everything; they want REALISTIC routed conduits with procedural material-aware support structures (brackets/gaskets/passthroughs picked by the wall material), copper for potable water (no synthetics), rigid tubes vs flexible (hoses/cords), and a clear/glass roof. The north star: 'holy shit this is all to code and all I did was play a video game.' I ran an Explore mapping the current model (rooms = RoomConfig AABBs in homestead_layout.ron; walls are IMPLICIT box-sides, not real entities; pipe routing is MATERIAL-BLIND + materials.csv is unused by it). KEY DECISION (operator's): node/wall construction (place corner nodes -> wall segments -> enclosed rooms), straight walls first. Operator SCOPED it tractably: FIXED outer box (55x89x3 m, all steel for now, fixed while aboard the mothership) + freely-designed INTERIOR WALLS; same tools for designing anything; built to be edited equally by an AI (the file) and a human (the editor). SHIPPED Stage 1 (data-model foundation, invisible by design): src/ship/home_structure.rs (HomeStructure{width,depth,height,shell_material,walls:Vec<InteriorWall{a,b,height,material}>} + RON load/save w/ header-preserve + generate_meshes -> the existing HomesteadMeshes (box shell + interior walls, drop-in render); reuses floor_quad+wall_box (now pub(crate))). data/blueprints/home_structure.ron = the 55x89x3 steel box. 4 unit tests + native + relay green.

**Why:** This is a strategic inflection -- the operator questioned the FOUNDATIONAL construction primitive, uncertain ('I'm not sure'). I did NOT barrel into building: validated the vision, mapped the current code (Explore) to ground a recommendation, recommended the node/wall model (matches their instinct + real-world + fixes the sliding/pass-through mess + unlocks the to-code plumbing), and got their direction + scope before building. The operator's fixed-box scoping made it tractable (the shell is a constant; the new work is the interior walls). Built Stage 1 as a CLEAN, AI+human-friendly model (one small readable RON file; add a wall = add a line) -- the 'works for AI and human' north star. Kept it invisible+tested (the operator agreed Stage 1 is the safe invisible data model) so nothing breaks; the risky wire+editor is Stage 2.

**Files:** src/ship/home_structure.rs, src/ship/fibonacci.rs, src/ship/mod.rs, data/blueprints/home_structure.ron


## 2026-06-24

**Decision:** HOME-CONSTRUCTION Stage 2a SHIPPED (v0.533.0): wall OPENINGS (doors/windows) with data-driven STYLES + mesh-gen cutting. The operator said 'build it' + mused about door ANIMATIONS (sliding/rotating/iris/energy/nanowall/organic) -- they want the door system extensible. The infinite-of-X answer: an opening's behavior/animation is a DATA-DRIVEN `style` string (swing/slide/iris/energy/nanowall/...), so new door kinds + their animations plug in later WITHOUT code; the future animation system reads the string. Added Opening{kind:Door|Window, at, width, sill, height, style} on InteriorWall (maps to the operator's vert model: a door is a point on the bottom edge; a window is a region) + wall_with_openings() which CUTS apertures out of the wall mesh (piers between/around openings + header + window sill; a full-size door leaves a clean gap). 5 unit tests; native+relay green. Also ANSWERED the operator's tessellation question (recorded in the commit + here): a flat wall does NOT need exploding into polygons -- per-pixel lighting + scaling the surface pattern to the wall's real size handle any size; only a split or an opening adds meaningful geometry; curves would need subdivision (later). This SIMPLIFIES the build (serves 'I want it easy').

**Why:** The operator refined the model to Blender-style verts/edges/faces (a wall = 4 verts; split; door = bottom-edge vert; window = 2-4 verts; machine = node) and asked a real technical question (is a huge polygon bad?). I reflected the model + gave the honest expertise (flat walls are fine; don't tessellate) -- which reduces complexity, the right service for 'make it easy'. Built the verifiable, NON-disruptive layer first (the opening model + mesh cutting, unit-tested) rather than ram the big visible render+editor rework blind at the tail of a marathon session -- that rework (Stage 2b) replaces the live home rendering + reworks construction.rs + re-homes machines, is 3D launch-verify-only, and is best done carefully with the operator available to verify. Built the door extensibility the operator just raised (their actual concern), so it's real forward progress on their ask, just on the safe layer.

**Files:** src/ship/home_structure.rs, data/blueprints/home_structure.ron
